WELL EVALUATION
Newfield Production Co.
Gariety 150-99-36-25-11H
SWSWSE SEC. 36 -T150N-R99W
McKenzie County, North Dakota
GENERAL:
Newfield Production Company's double section Gariety 150-99-36-25-11H
was "spudded" as a Three Forks Formation Double lateral well on July 8th, 2014. The subject
well is being drilled in the Watford Aquarium field, located about 4 mile South of Watford City
in McKenzie County, North Dakota. Surface location of the Gariety 150-99-36-25-11H is 325'
FSL, 2295' FEL, SWSWSE Section 36-T150N-R99W. The Gariety 150-99-36-25-11H was
planned with the ultimate goal of oil production in the dolomite porosity of the Three Forks
formation. The horizontal well-path was planned to follow structure with an estimated 90°
average formation dip throughout the lateral to total depth at 21,430.52' MD. The well bore was
planned with one 50 degree turn and finished with drilling to the North following an azimuth
along 0.0°.
ENGINEERING:
The Gariety 150-99-36-25-11H was drilled with Patterson UTI 346. Ground level of the
Gariety 150-99-36-25-11H was 2,163' above mean sea level with the Kelly bushing located at
2,188' above mean sea level, 25' above ground level.
The Gariety 150-99-36-25-11H was drilled with fresh water from surface to 2,225' MD.
A switch was then made and oil base mud, and was used from 2,225' MD to 11,555'MD. Once
horizontal, the well was switched over to salt brine from 11,555' MD to total depth at 21,422'
MD.
The main lateral of Newfield Production Company's Gariety 150-99-36-25-11H began
on August 9th, 2014. It was drilled from 11,555' MD (11,212' TVD) to a TD at 21,422' MD
(11,222.68'TVD, est). At TD a 5" liner was run in the vertical and 4.5" liner was ran through the
lateral and fracture stimulation was planned to enhance the well.
The final lateral profile for the Gariety 150-99-36-25-11H showed formation
dropping 17' TVD over a span of 9661.41' of vertical section drilled bringing the average dip for
the whole lateral to approximately 89.9 deg. The bottom hole location for the Gariety 150-99-36-
25-11H is 251' FNL,1064' FEL of NWNENE Sec 25 T150N R99W.
GEOLOGICAL EVALUATION:
Geologic supervision of the Newfield Production Company's Gariety 150-99-36-25-11H
well was provided by Geo-Link Geological Services with two-man geo-steering and geological
consulting service. Geologic evaluation began at a measured depth of 8,000' in the Minnelusa
Formation and continued until TD at the end of the lateral. An MSI Total Gas System model
TGC "Red Box" was used to record gas levels at the rigs shakers. The MSI model TGC was
integrated into Pason's EDR (Electronic Data Recorder) system. Also integrated into Pason's
EDR system was gamma data provided by Baker Hughes. Pason's EDR provided drill rate, total
gas, gamma and circulation data for viewing on location. Lagged samples for the well were
caught by the rig crews in 30' intervals from 8,000' through 11,555' and then 50' samples were
WELL EVALUATION
Newfield Production Co.
Gariety 150-99-36-25-11H
SWSWSE SEC. 36 -T150N-R99W
McKenzie County, North Dakota
caught until total depth was reached at 21,422' MD. Cuttings were examined under a binocular
microscope and UV fluoroscope. Cuttings were tested with 10% HCL acid solution and Alizarin
Red to distinguish between carbonates. Acetone was used to examine oil cut from the samples.
The samples were then photographed and logged in Mplot, Mud Logging Systems Inc. mud
logging program. After sample evaluation, one set of dried cuttings were saved for the State of
North Dakota.
The Charles Salt came in at 8,848' MD 8,847' TVD -6,659' sub-sea-level. The Charles
Salt consisted predominately of salts, limestone, and anhydrite. Salts from the Charles formation
were typically clear to translucent to translucent red in color, hard, massive, cubic and euhedral
crystalline structure, vitreous to sub glassy textures. Lithology below the salts in the Charles
formation consisted of limestone and anhydrites. Limestone's above the Ratcliffe interval within
the Charles formation were typically light gray to medium gray to bluish gray in color, firm to
brittle to hard, predominantly coarse to poor crystalline, wackestone, argillaceous, with poor
visible fracture porosity, no stain, no fluorescence, no odor, or cut fluorescence. No oil or gas
shows were observed while drilling the Charles Formation. No problems were encountered while
drilling the Charles Formation. The Base of the last Charles Salt was observed at 9,542' MD,
9,541' TVD and -7,353' sub-sea level.
The Mission Canyon formation top came in at 9,735' MD, 9,734' TVD and -7,546' sub-
sea level. The Mission Canyon formation consisted of gray limestones, moderately hard to hard
in hardness, cryptocrystalline wackestone to packstone in structure. Common shale inter-bedding
was observed. Poor to moderate oil show accompanied it in samples. Occasional lost circulation
intervals are found in the Mission Canyon. No other problems were encountered while drilling
the Mission Canyon formation.
The Lodgepole Formation top was recorded and observed at 10,283' MD, 10,282' TVD
and -8,094' sub-sea level. The Lodgepole Formation consisted of medium gray to gray to dark
brown to dark gray brown limestone, hard and microcrystalline to cryptocrystalline packstone
and wackestone in structure. No problems were encountered while drilling the Lodgepole
Formation.
The False Bakken top was recorded and observed at 11,165' MD, 11,089' TVD and -
8,901' sub-sea level. The False Bakken formation consisted of dark brown to dark gray limey
shale's. The shale's of the False Bakken were typically firm to brittle, sub-platy in structure, and
silty to earthy in texture. A 797 unit gas show was encountered while drilling the False Bakken
and had an oil show consisting of scattered faint yellow fluorescence with fast streaming blue
white cut fluorescence. No problems were encountered while drilling the False Bakken
formation.
The Upper Bakken Shale formation top was recorded and observed at 11,179' MD,
11,096' TVD and -8,908' sub-sea level. The Upper Bakken Shale's consisted of very dark gray
to black shale's, firm to soft to occasionally brittle in hardness, sub-blocky ­ blocky in structure,
carbonaceous to earthy in texture. Oil show was noted with drill cuttings of the Upper Bakken
Shale exhibiting a flash blue white cut fluorescence. A background gas increase was observed
WELL EVALUATION
Newfield Production Co.
Gariety 150-99-36-25-11H
SWSWSE SEC. 36 -T150N-R99W
McKenzie County, North Dakota
while drilling the Upper Bakken Shale with a peak gas recorded of 1,975 units. No problems
were encountered while drilling the Upper Bakken Shale.
The Middle Bakken dolomite top was recorded and observed at 11,210' MD, 11,116'
TVD and -8,928' sub-sea level. The Middle Bakken consisted of light gray to gray to tan to gray
brown dolomite. The Middle Bakken dolomite was typically soft to firm and occasionally brittle
in hardness, very fine crystalline packestone in structure, with crystalline to sub sucrosic
textures. Drill cuttings of the Middle Bakken showed good oil shows with even dull green to
yellow green fluorescence, faint to very strong hydrocarbon odors, moderately bright milky
bluish white flash cut with secondary multi-streaming cut fluorescence, and good visible
porosity. A peak gas level of 1477 units was recorded while drilling the Middle Bakken. No
problems were encountered while drilling the Middle Bakken.
The Lower Bakken shale top was recorded and observed at 11,283' measured depth,
11,154' true vertical depth and -8,966' sub-sea level. The Lower Bakken consisted of black
organic rich shale and silty shale. The Lower Bakken shale was typically soft to very soft blocky
carbonaceous shale, it is earthy to silty in texture with strong hydrocarbon odor and traces of
pyrite. The Lower Bakken shale had dull yellow fluorescence, streaming yellow cut as well as
bright yellow flash cut and a bright yellow residual cut ring. A peak gas show of 1928 units was
recorded in the Lower Bakken Shale. Gas was not run through the gas buster and no flare was
observed while drilling the Lower Bakken shale. No problems were encountered while drilling
the Lower Bakken shale.
The Pronghorn formation was recorded and observed at 11,318' measured depth, 11,170'
true vertical depth and -8,982' sub-sea level. The Pronghorn consisted of black to dark gray to
gray silty sandy shale to argillaceous limestone, The Pronghorn had little to know fluorescence,
streaming yellow cut as well as bright yellow flash cut and a bright yellow residual cut ring. A
gas show of 2657 units was encountered while drilling the Pronghorn.
The Three Forks top was recorded and observed at 11,381' measured depth, 11,192' true
vertical depth and -9,004' sub-sea level. The Three Forks consisted of light gray to gray to tan to
gray brown dolomite. The Three Forks dolomite was typically off white to gray to light gray to
white, hard to firm and occasionally soft in hardness, crystalline packestone in structure, with
coarse to intermittently coarse crystalline structure. Cuttings were slightly calcareous to limy as
you progressed deeper in zone. Cuttings showed poor to fair visible porosity and showed poor
oil shows with scattered dull yellow fluorescence, faint hydrocarbon odors, moderately bright
milky white to yellow flash cut with occasional secondary slow streaming cut fluorescence. The
Three Forks in this area also had a very prominent band of marine mudstone near the top of our
zone characterized by a high gamma peak. The marine mudstone was light blue green to blue
gray in color, firm to hard, crypto crystalline in structure. Cuttings are very slightly calcareous
have common interstitial pyrite, no visible porosity or oil show. Gas levels while drilling the
middle Bakken formation ranged from 500 units to 4155 units recorded by the ML TGC gas
detector. Gas was run through the gas buster starting at 12,480'. After going through the buster
gas levels dropped to 100 to 600 units and we had an intermittent 0-5' flare for the entire lateral
while drilling the Gariety 150-99-36-25-11H. The lateral was drilled 100% in the Three Forks,
WELL EVALUATION
Newfield Production Co.
Gariety 150-99-36-25-11H
SWSWSE SEC. 36 -T150N-R99W
McKenzie County, North Dakota
60% in zone and reached total depth of 21,422' MD on 9/8/2014 @ 21:56 hrs. Average dip for
the lateral was 89.9°.
SUMMARY:
Newfield Production Company's Gariety 150-99-36-25-11H was drilled successfully as a
double lateral into the Three Forks Formation. Gariety 150-99-36-25-11H took 25 days to drill
from "Spud" to TD.
Respectfully submitted by,
Josh Barcklay and Cory Turecek
Geo-Link Geological Services

RE:
HORIZONTAL WELL
GARIETY 150-99-36-25-11H
SWSE Section 36-150N-99W
McKenzie County
Well File # 28606
Dear Sarah:
Pursuant to Commission Order No. 23464, approval to drill the above captioned well is hereby given. The
approval is granted on the condition that all portions of the well bore not isolated by cement, be no closer than
the 200' setback from the north & south boundaries and 500' setback from the east & west boundaries within the
1280 acre spacing unit consisting of Sections 36 & 25 T150N-R99W.
PERMIT STIPULATIONS: Effective June 1, 2014, a covered leak-proof container (with placard) for
filter sock disposal must be maintained on the well site beginning when the well is spud, and must
remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations are
conducted. NEWFIELD PROD CO must contact NDIC Field Inspector Samuel Skurupey at 701-770-
1981 prior to location construction.
Drilling pit
NDAC 43-02-03-19.4 states that "a pit may be utilized to bury drill cuttings and solids generated during well
drilling and completion operations, providing the pit can be constructed, used and reclaimed in a manner that will
prevent pollution of the land surface and freshwaters. Reserve and circulation of mud system through earthen pits
are prohibited. All pits shall be inspected by an authorized representative of the director prior to lining and use.
Drill cuttings and solids must be stabilized in a manner approved by the director prior to placement in a cuttings
pit."
Form 1 Changes & Hard Lines
Any changes, shortening of casing point or lengthening at Total Depth must have prior approval by the NDIC.
The proposed directional plan is at a legal location. Based on the azimuth of the proposed lateral the maximum
legal coordinate from the well head is: 10031' north.
Location Construction Commencement (Three Day Waiting Period)
Operators shall not commence operations on a drill site until the 3rd business day following publication of the
approved drilling permit on the NDIC - OGD Daily Activity Report. If circumstances require operations to
commence before the 3rd business day following publication on the Daily Activity Report, the waiting period may
be waived by the Director. Application for a waiver must be by sworn affidavit providing the information
necessary to evaluate the extenuating circumstances, the factors of NDAC 43-02-03-16.2 (1), (a)-(f), and any other
information that would allow the Director to conclude that in the event another owner seeks revocation of the
drilling permit, the applicant should retain the permit.
Sarah King
June 12, 2014
Page 2
Permit Fee & Notification
Payment was received in the amount of $100 via credit card. It is requested that notification be given
immediately upon the spudding of the well. This information should be relayed to the Oil & Gas Division,
Bismarck, via telephone. The following information must be included: Well name, legal location, permit number,
drilling contractor, company representative, date and time of spudding. Office hours are 8:00 a.m. to 12:00 p.m.
and 1:00 p.m. to 5:00 p.m. Central Time. Our telephone number is (701) 328-8020, leave a message if after hours
or on the weekend.
Survey Requirements for Horizontal, Horizontal Re-entry, and Directional Wells
NDAC Section 43-02-03-25 (Deviation Tests and Directional Surveys) states in part (that) the survey
contractor shall file a certified copy of all surveys with the director free of charge within thirty days of completion.
Surveys must be submitted as one electronic copy, or in a form approved by the director. However, the director
may require the directional survey to be filed immediately after completion if the survey is needed to conduct the
operation of the director's office in a timely manner. Certified surveys must be submitted via email in one adobe
document, with a certification cover page to certsurvey@nd.gov.
Survey points shall be of such frequency to accurately determine the entire location of the well bore.
Specifically, the Horizontal and Directional well survey frequency is 100 feet in the vertical, 30 feet in the curve
(or when sliding) and 90 feet in the lateral.
Confidential status
Your request for confidential status of all information furnished to the Director, or his representatives, is
hereby granted. Such information, except production runs, shall remain confidential for six months commencing
on the date the well is spud.
Confidential status notwithstanding, the Director and his representatives shall have access to all well
records wherever located. Your company personnel, or any person performing work for your company shall
permit the Director and his representatives to come upon any lease, property, well, or drilling rig operated or
controlled by them, complying with all safety rules, and to inspect the records and operation of such wells and to
have access at all times to any and all records of wells. The Commission's field personnel periodically inspect
producing and drilling wells. Any information regarding such wells shall be made available to them at any time
upon request. The information so obtained by the field personnel shall be maintained in strict confidence and
shall be available only to the Commission and its staff.
Surface casing cement
Tail cement utilized on surface casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi within 12
hours, and tail cement utilized on production casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi
before drilling the plug or initiating tests.
Logs NDAC Section 43-02-03-31 requires the running of (1) a suite of open hole logs from which formation tops and
porosity zones can be determined, (2) a Gamma Ray Log run from total depth to ground level elevation of the well bore, and
(3) a log from which the presence and quality of cement can be determined (Standard CBL or Ultrasonic cement evaluation
log) in every well in which production or intermediate casing has been set, this log must be run prior to completing the well.
All logs run must be submitted free of charge, as one digital TIFF (tagged image file format) copy and one digital LAS (log
ASCII) formatted copy. Digital logs may be submitted on a standard CD, DVD, or attached to an email sent to
digitallogs@nd.gov Thank you for your cooperation.
Sincerely,
Nathaniel Erbele
Petroleum Resource Specialist

Petroleum Resource Specialist
April 9, 2014
RE:
Filter Socks and Other Filter Media
Leakproof Container Required
Oil and Gas Wells
Dear Operator,
North Dakota Administrative Code Section 43-02-03-19.2 states in part that all waste material associated with
exploration or production of oil and gas must be properly disposed of in an authorized facility in accord with all
applicable local, state, and federal laws and regulations.
Filtration systems are commonly used during oil and gas operations in North Dakota. The Commission is very
concerned about the proper disposal of used filters (including filter socks) used by the oil and gas industry.
Effective June 1, 2014, a container must be maintained on each well drilled in North Dakota beginning when the
well is spud and must remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations
are conducted. The on-site container must be used to store filters until they can be properly disposed of in an
authorized facility. Such containers must be:
leakproof to prevent any fluids from escaping the container
covered to prevent precipitation from entering the container
placard to indicate only filters are to be placed in the container
If the operator will not utilize a filtration system, a waiver to the container requirement will be considered, but
only upon the operator submitting a Sundry Notice (Form 4) justifying their request.
As previously stated in our March 13, 2014 letter, North Dakota Administrative Code Section 33-20-02.1-01
states in part that every person who transports solid waste (which includes oil and gas exploration and production
wastes) is required to have a valid permit issued by the North Dakota Department of Health, Division of Waste
Management. Please contact the Division of Waste Management at (701) 328-5166 with any questions on the
solid waste program. Note oil and gas exploration and production wastes include produced water, drilling mud,
invert mud, tank bottom sediment, pipe scale, filters, and fly ash.
Thank you for your cooperation.
Sincerely,
Bruce E. Hicks
Assistant Director
Gariety 150-99-36-25-11H
SWSWSE S36 T150N R99W
McKenzie County, North Dakota
To whom it may concern:
This notice is intended to confirm that the proposed completion consisting of hydraulic fracture treatment
on the above mentioned well is in compliance with EPA UIC Program Guidance #84 dated February
2014 regarding oil and gas hydraulic fracturing activities using diesel fuels. Newfield is aware of the EPA
guidance and does not intend to inject "diesel fuels" in any quantity. Newfield has confirmed with its
fracturing service provider that diesel fuels are not included in the chemicals injected during fracturing
treatment of Newfield operated wells. Diesel fuels are defined below by Chemical Abstract Service
Registry Number:
1) 68334-30-5 Primary Name: Fuels, diesel
2) 68476-34-6 Primary Name: Fuels, diesel, No. 2
3) 68476-30-2 Primary Name: Fuel oil No. 2
4) 68476-31-3 Primary Name: Fuel oil, No. 4
5) 8008-20-6 Primary Name: Kerosene
In anticipation of EPA's diesel fuel guidance that was in development for several years, Newfield had
already prohibited the use of diesel fuels in our hydraulic fracturing fluids systems. This self-imposed
prohibition was clarified with formal notices to our respective pressure pumping service providers.
Newfield discloses all of our chemicals pumped to the Ground Water Protection Council's national
registry FracFocus and voluntarily submitted 25 wells in North Dakota before the April 1, 2012 effective
date of North Dakota Administrative Code 43-02-03-27.1.g.
